Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2281671,"date":"2022-03-09T04:00:26","date_gmt":"2022-03-09T12:00:26","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281671"},"modified":"2022-03-08T12:14:28","modified_gmt":"2022-03-08T20:14:28","slug":"silq-spins-its-technology-into-visibility-for-apparel-manufacturing","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/09\/silq-spins-its-technology-into-visibility-for-apparel-manufacturing\/","title":{"rendered":"Silq spins its technology into visibility for apparel manufacturing"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The clothing industry is often called out for not being socially responsible, and Ram Radhakrishnan, CEO of <a href=\"https:\/\/www.onesilq.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Silq<\/a>, says brands have a hard time finding a factory that meets quality and capability requirements while also being transparent in communication.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe problem is not a lack of technology, but a lack of structured data,\u201d he told TechCrunch. \u201cNone of the solutions have solved the problem yet, and the global pandemic exacerbated it.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Radhakrishnan, who started the company with Kate Alexander and Vishnu Nair, spent years in India observing family members running factories, which ultimately inspired the idea for Silq. He came to the United States and worked in transportation, including stints at both C.H. Robinson and Flexport.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281671\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>He noted that $2.8 trillion worth of merchandise came into the U.S. in the last year, and some $500 billion was spent in fixing supply chain inefficiencies, something he attributes to the inflation we are seeing now. In addition, companies are trying to get supply chain data, but have not been able to.<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s where his company is stepping in with its approach to bring visibility and real-time data from the manufacturing floor to brands. Its technology helps users source, make and ship apparel, footwear, home goods and accessory brands.<\/p>\n<p>In fact, Silq puts its own employees on the ground in facilities to provide updates during the production process that results in improved product quality and accelerated speed-to-market. The company provides brands with a production calendar designed and maintained by Silq.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe show them what is happening on supply chain floors and provide validated data from people on site in five countries,\u201d Radhakrishnan said. \u201cUsing the data, customers can make freight bookings because we can predict what will happen up to 45 days in advance.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The company was in beta mode for half of 2021, but managed to bring in $10 million in gross merchandise value from the five countries it operates in.<\/p>\n<p>Silq is focused on soft goods currently, but will move into broader categories of consumer goods in 2022.<\/p>\n<p>It is also leveraging growth in markets it is not operating in, including Asia and Latin America, but Radhakrishnan expects to have a presence in those regions by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>That growth is buoyed by $17.6 million in new Series A funding, co-led by F-Prime Capital and Flexport Ventures. Joining in the round were Eight Roads Ventures, existing investors RTP Seed and Forum Ventures and a group of angel investors. It gives the company approximately $19.6 million in total funding to date. As part of the round, Ben Gorman of F-Prime Capital joins the board.<\/p>\n<p>Radhakrishnan plans to use the new funding to expand its footprint of factory partners around the world, grow its team of on-site merchandisers and quality inspectors across Asia and invest in technology development.<\/p>\n<p>Speaking to the current bottleneck going on in the supply chain, Radhakrishnan said he doesn\u2019t expect it to be clear until summer 2024.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe don\u2019t have infrastructure to handle throughput, so either we build some or it has to decrease,\u201d he added. \u201cBuilding infrastructure doesn&#8217;t happen overnight, so the thing we can hope for is improving efficiency within the existing infrastructure, and that is what Silq does. This is going to have to happen in the next five years because infrastructure will take half a decade to build. Until then, any efficiency is going to come from solutions like us and others to leverage existing assets.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"M4rEmwxwbw\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/6-tips-for-establishing-your-startups-global-supply-chain\/\">6 tips for establishing your startup&#8217;s global supply america","slug":"latin-america","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/5839"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=5839"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=5839"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=5839"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=5839"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576992454,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ram-radhakrishnan\/","name":"Ram Radhakrishnan","slug":"ram-radhakrishnan","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576992454"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576992454"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576992454"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576992454"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576992454"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2281041,"date":"2022-03-08T06:35:36","date_gmt":"2022-03-08T14:35:36","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281041"},"modified":"2022-03-08T06:34:19","modified_gmt":"2022-03-08T14:34:19","slug":"swiftly-brick-and-mortar-stores-online-customers","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/swiftly-brick-and-mortar-stores-online-customers\/","title":{"rendered":"Swiftly quickly gets brick-and-mortar stores set up to cater to online customers"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Much of the technology attention lately has been paid to e-commerce companies, driven in large part by brick-and-mortar stores having to close for some time during the global pandemic. However, some companies, like retail technology company <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swiftly.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Swiftly<\/a>, want to give those retailers a chance to capture similar customer experiences, loyalty and digital advertising dollars.<\/p>\n<p>When we spoke to co-founder and CEO Henry Kim <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/24\/building-a-creator-focused-os\/\">last April<\/a>, he was focused on helping grocery chains go digital, a slice of the market that accounted for <a href=\"https:\/\/www.supermarketnews.com\/online-retail\/e-commerce-account-20-us-grocery-market-2026\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">9.5% of total U.S. grocery sales<\/a> in 2021, but is expected to grow to 20.5% in 2026. The company had raised $15 million to date and had just announced a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.grocerydive.com\/news\/dollar-tree-launches-a-retail-media-network\/598486\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">deal with Dollar Tree<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe knew that over the past 20 years a disproportionate share of the venture capital dollars went to e-commerce businesses, while comparatively few venture dollars were invested in tools to help brick-and-mortar retailers,\u201d Kim told TechCrunch. \u201cIf you look at the split of how Americans buy, even today, over 80% of purchases still happen in a brick-and-mortar store.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281041\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Swiftly provides the technology tools that Kim says \u201cdemocratizes the technology lead, enjoyed by Amazon and Walmart, to the rest of the industry,\u201d like mobile technology capabilities to engage shoppers digitally and make shopping in-store as easy as online, while also providing analytics and advertising, so that they can compete against e-commerce retailers using their operational strength without being disadvantaged by an aging or non-existing technology platform.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"siDUlZOSCH\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/24\/building-a-creator-focused-os\/\">Building a creator-focused OS<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Building a creator-focused OS&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/24\/building-a-creator-focused-os\/embed\/#?secret=2jtYyIcENf#?secret=siDUlZOSCH\" data-secret=\"siDUlZOSCH\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Since its seed round in 2018, the company has more than doubled in size with a focus on hiring in engineering, product, sales and marketing. It also rounded out the leadership team to include a CRO, CFO and vice presidents of retailer growth, engineering and business development.<\/p>\n<p>Swiftly is being used by hundreds of consumer brands in nearly 10,000 store locations, which accounts for more than $30 billion in gross merchandise volume.<\/p>\n<p>Today, the company is back with an even bigger round of funding, a $100 million Series B led by Wormhole Capital, to give it $120 million in total funding. The round also included Liquid2 Ventures, Bramalea, Gaingels, Silicon Ventures, Proof VC, Western Technology Investment, Sand Hill Angels and The Martin Family. Kim did not reveal Swiftly\u2019s valuation.<\/p>\n<p>This raise was always part of the plan, and Kim says it \u201csets Swiftly up for the next level of scale as we deploy across the next million retail stores across the world.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In addition to making investments in engineering, sales and marketing, and technology infrastructure, the new capital will be used to expand into new verticals outside of grocery retail, for example, beauty, home improvement and sporting goods.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281042\" style=\"width: 210px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281042\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2281042\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Swiftly-App.png?w=150\" alt=\"Swiftly\" width=\"200\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Swiftly-App.png 180w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Swiftly-App.png?resize=75,150 75w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Swiftly-App.png?resize=150,300 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Swiftly-App.png?resize=25,50 25w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281042\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Swiftly app. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Swiftly<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Kim says the future of e-commerce will be \u201cwho owns the customer.\u201d And from Swiftly\u2019s research, consumers and brands would still invest their money in a brick-and-mortar store that has anchored their community for years.<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s because traditional retailers can employ digital tools for recapturing customers faster than Amazon can build 3,000 grocery stores, something the company already tried to do with bookstores, but <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/amazon-to-close-68-physical-retail-locations-including-amazon-books-and-4-star-stores\/\">decided last week to close them<\/a>, citing a challenging in-person shopping environment due to the pandemic.<\/p>\n<p>However, other startups are taking Swiftly\u2019s position and making similar bets that in-store will continue to dominate as investors come along for the ride. For example, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/11\/foxtrot-convenience-store-of-the-future\/\">Foxtrot<\/a> is developing digital experiences for convenience stores.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIn the next two years, you\u2019re going to see brick-and-mortar retailers leverage their advantages like the convenience of their store locations, the fact that most grocery products are cheaper when purchased in the store rather than online and the personalization opportunities afforded by mobile technology to develop their own competitive advantage,\u201d Kim added.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GOASAZDuTM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/03\/11-ways-to-make-personalized-shopping-more-effective-and-profitable\/\">11 ways to make personalized shopping more effective and profitable<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" invests $128M into expansion of Saltbox&#8217;s warehouse, co-working spaces for entrepreneurs"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.saltbox.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Saltbox<\/a>, a company providing co-working and warehousing space for up-and-coming e-commerce businesses, said it is working with Fundrise, a real estate investment firm, to expand nationally.<\/p>\n<p>We covered Saltbox\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/15\/saltbox-raises-10-6m-to-help-booming-ecommerce-stores-store-their-goods\/\">$10.6 million Series A<\/a> round last year and spoke to CEO Tyler Scriven about the company\u2019s first facility, a 27,000-square-foot location in Atlanta, opened in 2019, which was at capacity in a span of two months. That was followed by a bigger space in the Dallas-Fort Worth area.<\/p>\n<p>Fundrise is putting $128 million into the effort, which is part of its larger strategy to invest in well-located, last-mile logistics industrial real estate.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281058\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>As part of the investment, Fundrise will acquire warehouses ranging in size from 50,000 to 150,000 square feet that will house the new Saltbox locations. The first two locations will be in Alexandria, Virginia and Atlanta, which will give it two in that city. Saltbox also just recently added a location in Phoenix.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cOne of the eloquent things about the partnership with Fundrise is their business model of democratizing access to real estate for retail investors,\u201d Scriven said. \u201cIn our case, Saltbox is democratizing access to logistic infrastructure for small businesses, like retail customers, so we have a shared conceptual approach to the markets we are serving.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The businesses using Saltbox\u2019s facilities have $200 billion worth of e-commerce gross merchandise volume attributed to them, a figure he expects to be $500 billion in the next eight years.<\/p>\n<p>Though those companies are given thousands of tools to help grow their business, like Shopify, Stripe and Facebook, the aspect of e-commerce logistics continues to be \u201chard and messy,\u201d with most infrastructure not built for small businesses. As a result, most are stuck fulfilling orders from basements, garages and storage spaces when what they really need is a warehouse, Scriven said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe bring that together with an end-to-end solution, and at the crux of our strategy is human-centric logistics,\u201d he added.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Saltbox has six locations currently, with plans to have 15 by the end of this year.<\/p>\n<p>Brandon Jenkins, COO of Fundrise, told TechCrunch that his company liked the approach Saltbox was taking to open up access to real estate. The company typically invests in residential apartments, but is also bullish on industrial.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe real estate we are looking at is where there is a lot of growth and more activity,\u201d Jenkins said. \u201cSaltbox is doing industrial in an interesting way, mashing up asset classes and companies and coming at it from a new direction. This was a unique way we brought partnership together \u2014 it is usually not done in this way.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" management","slug":"supply-chain-management","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576827979"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576827979"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576827979"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576827979"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576827979"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576873665,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/tyler-scriven\/","name":"Tyler Scriven","slug":"tyler-scriven","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576873665"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576873665"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576873665"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576873665"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576873665"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2281028,"date":"2022-03-08T03:00:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-08T11:00:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281028"},"modified":"2022-03-07T13:37:00","modified_gmt":"2022-03-07T21:37:00","slug":"zapt-trela-food-shopping","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/zapt-trela-food-shopping\/","title":{"rendered":"Zapt is now Trela; aims to remove the middleman from group food shopping"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">People who purchase as a group, for anything from insurance to a group of neighbors fixing their fence, can often command a better purchase deal.<\/p>\n<p>In Trela\u2019s case, it is developing a way for Brazilian neighbors to connect groups of people to suppliers, particularly for food purchases with the goal of eliminating the middleman so purchases can be made directly.<\/p>\n<p>The social commerce company, formerly known as Zapt, was founded in 2020 by Guilherme Nazareth, Guilherme Alvarenga and Jo\u00e3o J\u00f6nk. Prior to that, Nazareth was a data scientist in San Francisco, and when he saw the dollar skyrocket, he thought it was an exciting opportunity to move back to Brazil and start a company in a large, fragmented market that had tailwinds from the global pandemic.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281028\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThat\u2019s how I landed on food,\u201d he added. \u201cThe Brazilian grocery market was fragmented, so I drove around with a beer salesperson to find out what kind of technology they needed.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"e38R145N40\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/20\/from-farm-to-phone-a-paradigm-shift-in-grocery\/\">From farm to phone: A paradigm shift in grocery<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;From farm to phone: A paradigm shift in grocery&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/20\/from-farm-to-phone-a-paradigm-shift-in-grocery\/embed\/#?secret=gfwAIT5vXQ#?secret=e38R145N40\" data-secret=\"e38R145N40\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The inspiration for Trela came shortly after that, when Nazareth met a company CTO who had created data around his neighbor buying directly from suppliers. \u201cThere was a full WhatsApp group and a 100% waitlist. That\u2019s when I saw a new consumer experience banging on the door and wanted to create a product that let behavior like that be prevalent.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Trela\u2019s social commerce marketplace enables neighbors to buy premium products from the supplier without a middleman, in a more efficient and fair way than the grocery store, and at lower prices for the products and delivery.<\/p>\n<p>Nazareth explained that the company is competing against grocery stores by connecting the ends of the supply chain to give neighbors themselves the buying power of a small restaurant or grocery store so that they can share in the cost of food \u2014 in some cases between 20%. and 60% in lower costs.<\/p>\n<p>On the supplier side, they can command a better margin, Nazareth said. It also is connected to WhatsApp, which allows Trela to gamify the experience and update products in real time.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Here\u2019s how it works: In the Trela group, users get a new offer or update on an offer for food items, and when the user clicks on the link, it takes them over to the web app where they can check out in one click. If you want to create a group, you can be nominated to do so, and Trela will reach out. Most of the group creators are foodies and those who bring their neighborhoods together. Users also can ask for product recommendations.<\/p>\n<p>Nazareth and his co-founders launched the product in 2021, and after being a part of Y Combinator\u2019s Winter 2021 cohort, they raised a seed round. Today, they announced $25 million in Series A funding, touting it as one of the largest Series A rounds in Latin America.<\/p>\n<p>The round was led by SoftBank Latin America and included Kaszek, General Catalyst, Y Combinator and Pierpaolo Barbieri. Including the new funds, Trela has raised $27.8 million in total.<\/p>\n<p>Since the seed round in April 2021, the company has grown 30 times in revenue and is seeing an average growth of 45% per month, Nazareth said. That includes going from nine employees at the time to 32. Trela currently operates in S\u00e3o Paulo and Belo Horizonte, and he expects to be in another five cities by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019ve been a scrappy seed and have a million things to do,\u201d he added. As a result, most of the new funding will go into product development and hiring. Suppliers are responsible for the deliveries right now, but Trela is testing its own deliveries, which Nazareth says has been successful so far and will be rolled out further.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"8xW4SUJOhY\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/01\/whos-building-the-grocery-store-of-the-future\/\">Who&#8217;s building the grocery store of the future?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Who&#8217;s building the grocery store of the future?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/01\/whos-building-the-grocery-store-of-the-future\/embed\/#?secret=Y2p7HZ9OYM#?secret=8xW4SUJOhY\" data-secret=\"8xW4SUJOhY\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" buying food for their neighbors directly from suppliers rather than the grocery Barbieri","slug":"pierpaolo-barbieri","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576909599"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576909599"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576909599"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576909599"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576909599"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2280310,"date":"2022-03-07T04:00:47","date_gmt":"2022-03-07T12:00:47","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2280310"},"modified":"2022-03-04T14:57:52","modified_gmt":"2022-03-04T22:57:52","slug":"cayena-delivers-inventory-marketplace-for-food-preparation-businesses","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/cayena-delivers-inventory-marketplace-for-food-preparation-businesses\/","title":{"rendered":"Cayena delivers inventory marketplace for food preparation businesses"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Procuring items to fill the shelves of local stores is not an easy task in Latin America. Orders are mostly still done on paper or over the phone, and sometimes store owners have to drive to the wholesaler to get their orders.<\/p>\n<p>Cayena founders Gabriel Sendacz, Pedro Carvalho and Raymond Shayo believe injecting technology into procurement will make the process much simpler for food preparation facilities, like restaurants, bars, bakeries, hotels and dark kitchens, in their home country of Brazil and across the region.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cLatin American B2B is a massive market, but it is fragmented when it comes to supply and demand,\u201d Shayo told TechCrunch. \u201cAbout 90% of our customers are small and medium, independent and family-owned businesses. On the supplier side, there are thousands of distributors all with different products, but they have less than 1% of the market share.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280310\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>In contrast, the United States has large foodservice companies, like Sysco, U.S. Foods and Gordon Food Service, which hold around <a href=\"https:\/\/msourceideas.com\/explaining-food-industry-wholesale-distributors\/#:~:text=Types%20of%20Food%20Distributors&amp;text=In%20the%20US%2C%20the%20industry,host%20of%20smaller%2C%20regional%20players.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">10% market share<\/a> and offer a one-stop shop for everything from food to cleaning supplies.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FZ2sz05slh\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/17\/what-does-brazils-new-receivables-regulation-mean-for-fintechs\/\">What does Brazil&#8217;s new receivables regulation mean for fintechs?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;What does Brazil&#8217;s new receivables regulation mean for fintechs?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/17\/what-does-brazils-new-receivables-regulation-mean-for-fintechs\/embed\/#?secret=8qdLLS5krU#?secret=FZ2sz05slh\" data-secret=\"FZ2sz05slh\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2280318\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2280318\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2280318\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png\" alt=\"Pedro Carvalho, Gabriel Sendacz, Raymond Shayo\" width=\"1024\" height=\"506\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png 3456w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png?resize=150,74 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png?resize=680,336 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png?resize=1536,759 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png?resize=2048,1012 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/PedroCarvalho.GabrielSendacz.RaymojndShayo.png?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2280318\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cayena co-founders, from left, Pedro Carvalho, Gabriel Sendacz and Raymond Shayo. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cayena<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>As a result, there are several problems Shayo explained, including that across 20 vendors there might be a 40% to 50% difference in price for the same item. It can also take credit card companies around 30 days to pay restaurants, but at the same time, restaurants have to pay in advance for their inventory orders, which results in a working capital problem, especially when ingredients are the largest cost for restaurants, he added.<\/p>\n<p>Simply put, it is easy for restaurants in Latin America to get behind and stay behind. So they created a business-to-business marketplace, targeting the $100 billion wholesale food industry in Latin America, that enables users to source inventory from multiple suppliers at one time and get orders delivered the next day. It is also offering add-on services like buy now, pay later financing.<\/p>\n<p>Users can browse through the products and get a quote on the selected items. Cayena\u2019s algorithm takes into account what is available from the suppliers and the user\u2019s budget and provides the best combination of suppliers. The company utilizes a drop-ship model for delivery and once the order is made notifies the suppliers to deliver the order.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>After launching the marketplace in 2020, the company saw its customer base grow 10 times in one year and average ticket sizes multiplied by four times, as it became harder for restaurants to procure inventories, with the average customer purchasing from Cayena five times a month.<\/p>\n<p>That prompted the company to go after additional capital, including a <a href=\"https:\/\/latamlist.com\/cayena-foodtech-raises-3-5m-series-a-funding-round\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$3.5 million round<\/a> in late 2021 led by Picus Capital, after initially raising $550,000 in a round led by Canary.<\/p>\n<p>Business was so good that shortly after the seed round in September, the founders saw Cayena double in growth and keep that pace every two months or so as it reached a milestone of R$100 million, or nearly $200 million, in annualized transaction volume across its presence in 50 cities in the state of S\u00e3o Paulo.<\/p>\n<p>All of that acceleration caught the attention of investors, and the company was preempted with a $17.5 million Series A investment, led by Vine Ventures, that also included participation from MSA Capital, Picus Capital, Canaan Partners, Clocktower Ventures, FJ Labs, Femsa Ventures, Gilgamesh, Astella, Endeavor and GraoVC. This gives Cayena just over $21 million in total funding.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt is a very hot market right now, which is a good thing because it has become easier for investors all over the world to compare and benchmark which companies are successful,\u201d Shayo said. \u201cA few years ago, it was hard to compare, but it is clear who is taking different approaches and strategies now.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Due to its business model, Cayena doesn\u2019t need to invest in warehouse, trucks or distribution, just the technology, so much of the new capital will go into hiring. Shayo expects to double the team of 60 by the end of the year. The company will also focus on product and technology to create new financial products and expand geographic suppliers.<\/p>\n<p>Next up, the founders see opportunity in Latin America as a whole, so future plans are to first scale toward being the largest food services supplier in Brazil, without having a single truck, in the next one to three years, then expand around the region.<\/p>\n<div Sendacz","slug":"gabriel-sendacz","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576990761"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576990761"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576990761"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576990761"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576990761"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2279708,"date":"2022-03-04T05:00:52","date_gmt":"2022-03-04T13:00:52","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2279708"},"modified":"2022-03-03T15:50:12","modified_gmt":"2022-03-03T23:50:12","slug":"disco-gets-brands-to-boogie-together-on-customer-acquisition","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/disco-gets-brands-to-boogie-together-on-customer-acquisition\/","title":{"rendered":"Disco gets brands to boogie together on customer acquisition"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As more companies establish an e-commerce presence, the stakes have never been higher for brands to cut through the clutter to land new customers.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.disconetwork.com\/\">Disco<\/a>, formerly known as Co-op Commerce, doesn\u2019t think the cost of acquiring costs should be so reliant on Big Tech platforms. Instead, Conner Sherline, founder and CEO, says that when independent brands come together across partnerships, data and merchandising, they have the buying power to produce results for everyone.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2279740\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2279740\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2279740\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?w=200\" alt=\"Conner Sherline, disco\" width=\"300\" height=\"451\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg 2683w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=100,150 100w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=200,300 200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=768,1154 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=452,680 452w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=1022,1536 1022w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=1363,2048 1363w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Conner-Sherline_headshot.jpg?resize=33,50 33w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2279740\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Conner Sherline, founder and CEO of Disco. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Disco<\/p><\/div><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2279708\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The new name was actually one that Sherline had been thinking about before the company was Co-op Commerce. The leadership team decided to change the name because the company was not a co-op, and with its focus on \u201cdiscovery,\u201d Sherline explained it fit more with helping consumers find the next thing within its network and cutting through the noise. Relating to discovery on the merchant side, it was also discovering new things about customers and other merchants.<\/p>\n<p>When we talked to Sherline last August for the company\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/29\/co-op-raises-5-8m-round-to-help-online-merchants-land-customers-for-less\/\">$5.8 million round<\/a>, 500 brands were part of Disco\u2019s ecosystem that streamlines the collaboration, tracking and marketplace data that the brands can use to make better decisions around their marketing and merchandising.<\/p>\n<p>This approach has now gained traction. In its first year of business, Disco saw more than $1 billion of transactions across its brand network and over 40 million shoppers as brands experienced 30% to 50% lower costs than on platforms like Facebook and Instagram, Sherline said.<\/p>\n<p>The company\u2019s first full year in business was 2021, and during that time, the company\u2019s revenue grew 10 times, while average contract value and revenue per customer values are higher because Disco is able to reduce the acquisition costs that gobble up much of a brand\u2019s revenue.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Disco is now working with large brands in direct-to-consumer, including The Honest Company, Parade, Lovevery, Made In, Girlfriend Collective, Faherty, Lunya, Rhone, Caraway and Milk Bar.<\/p>\n<p>And, it has another round of funding, this time raising $20 million Series A funding led by Felicis Ventures. Participating in the round were Shopify, Sugar Capital, Bessemer Venture Partners, Indicator Ventures, RiverPark Ventures, Vibe Capital, Not Boring Fund and a group of DTC founders and operators. To date, Disco has raised $26 million.<\/p>\n<p>The new round was preempted, but came at a good time for the company, Sherline said. A cookie-less future is inevitable, but the challenge he is seeing is that companies have not had time to react or respond, and the solution is for brands to work together to lower customer acquisition costs while also improving the targeting of customers.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWith everything happening, including iOS 15 hampering businesses to effectively do marketing and Facebook being less effective in driving acquisition costs, this is our moment to shine and bring on more people to the team to go after a larger opportunity,\u201d he added. \u201cBecause we work with brands directly and sit on larger sets of consumer data, we are able to close that loop without cookies.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The new capital will enable the company to grow its team. Sherline aims to go from 27 employees to 75 by the end of the year. Disco will also be testing more business-to-business marketing and getting its own marketing funnel set up to build leads.<\/p>\n<p>Now armed with its new funding, Disco joins other startups, like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/30\/flip-bags-28m-to-turn-beauty-wellness-social-commerce-on-its-head\/\">Flip<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/bloomreach-customer-personalization\/\">Bloomreach<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/stop-guessing-your-kpis-varos-shows-e-commerce-saas-companies-how-you-compare-to-peers\/\">Varos<\/a>, to attract funding to provide their own approaches to customer acquisition.<\/p>\n<p>Niki Pezeshki, general partner at Felicis, said Disco caught his eye having been an early investor in Shopify and a dozen e-commerce brands over the years. Those investments gave Felicis firsthand insights to the struggles of user acquisition, which he said had become more expensive over the past five years.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhen we heard from Conner, we were excited about the market he was going after, the problem they were solving and that Shopify was already an investor,\u201d Pezeshki said. \u201cDTC is growing faster than everyone else. Shopify is a bigger marketplace, but not focused on the advertising space, or customer acquisition, which is left to social media and search engines. Disco is coming in and solving that for all of those for DTC brands.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"0BVeo4LZDe\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/09\/how-to-acquire-customer-research-that-shapes-your-go-to-market-strategy\/\">How to acquire customer research that shapes your go-to-market
