cooks up creator partnership approach to digitally native, local food brands"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">To create the perfect recipe of new food brands and experiences, <a href=\"http:\/\/popchew.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Popchew<\/a> has compiled a list of infrastructure and restaurant partnership ingredients so that creators can build, launch and grow their own local, digitally native food brands nationally in a matter of weeks.<\/p>\n<p>The New York startup was founded in 2021 by Rushir Parikh and Nick Sopchak and in the company\u2019s first six months, launched two brands, Bitcoin Pizza with investor Anthony &#8220;Pomp&#8221; Pompliano and Wing SZN in partnership with YouTuber Zias. They are available for delivery via third-party apps and the Popchew website.<\/p>\n<p>The idea for the company stemmed from Parikh\u2019s childhood growing up working at his uncle\u2019s restaurant and Sopchak\u2019s background in the hospitality industry. They felt food was fun, but that the $40 billion food delivery market could be opened up to help creators expand their personal brand, connect with fans and create a new revenue stream.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2279777\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe realized that the way we are eating is evolving and it is turning into content,\u201d Parikh told TechCrunch. \u201cYou see food everywhere on Instagram and TikTok, and we felt the future of food could be creators. However, it is hard for creators to get into food unless they are a mega celebrity working with a food company.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Here\u2019s how it works: Creators figure out the type of food they want to sell, and Popchew brings that idea to life through digital experiences where friends can come together around food \u2014 see what they\u2019ve ordered and send food to friends. On the restaurant side, Popchew taps into restaurants&#8217; unused capacity and helps creators optimize it to create another revenue stream. All of the orders flow through the company and its splits the proceeds between the creators and restaurants.<\/p>\n<p>The company has partnerships with more than 100 restaurants currently, but Parikh says with over 600,000 restaurants in the U.S., brands can expand reach without changing restaurants\u2019 existing operation.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2279783\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2279783\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2279783\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg\" alt=\"Popchew, WingSZN\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg 8688w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WingSZN.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2279783\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Popchew&#8217;s Wing SZN brand. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Popchew<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Parikh and Sopchak are also toying with the idea of enabling parents to load up Popchew accounts for their college-aged children for food delivery. Users earn a loyalty point for every dollar spent, which then can be used to purchase prizes from the creators, for example, an appearance on their YouTube video or merchandise.<\/p>\n<p>A pilot in May for Bitcoin Pizza Day took place in 10 cities and pulled in $100,000 in gross merchandise volume in the first seven days. Since then, Popchew has processed tens of thousands of orders and is poised to generate several million dollars in revenue by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>The company has plans to launch new brands every month with its roster of creators, and to reach that goal, secured $3.6 million in seed funding. Long Journey Ventures led the round and was joined by Jake Paul\u2019s Anti Fund, Flybridge, WndrCo, the Uber Alumni Syndicate and a group of strategic angel investors, including Rus Yusupov of HQ Trivia and Vine, Steven Galanis of Cameo, Rich Antoniello of Complex Media, Scott Belsky, Pompliano and Matteo Franceschetti.<\/p>\n<p>The capital infusion will enable the company to build on its core food experiences and invest in product, engineering and operations.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cFood is the authentic way to engage with audiences,\u201d Sopchak said. \u201cOur approach provides an incremental line of revenue for creators and restaurants, so it is mutually beneficial.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Popchew is the latest startup to attract capital for its approach to helping people create food brands. For example, in 2020, Disha Gulati and Nicholas Florek tapped into $800,000 in pre-seed to get <a href=\"https:\/\/hereheremarket.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Here Here Market<\/a> going to feature local food gift boxes from up-and-coming culinary creators. In the past year, we also saw <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/dishdivvy-serves-up-marketplace-for-on-demand-home-cooked-food\/\">DishDivvy<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/10\/woodspoons-food-delivery-service-cooks-up-support-for-home-chefs-with-14m-round\/\">WoodSpoon<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/02\/shef-raises-20m-to-expand-its-homemade-meal-delivery-marketplace\/\">Shef<\/a> raise funds to help home cooks create a revenue stream with their homemade creations.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FQjcKMpcTf\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/4-trends-that-will-define-e-commerce-in-2022\/\">4 trends that will define e-commerce in 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2279119,"date":"2022-03-03T08:00:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-03T16:00:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2279119"},"modified":"2022-03-04T05:39:50","modified_gmt":"2022-03-04T13:39:50","slug":"nzvc-new-zealand-ventures","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/03\/nzvc-new-zealand-ventures\/","title":{"rendered":"NZVC creates fund for early-stage New Zealand ventures"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Mark Pavlyukovskyy, Ajay Gupta and Glen Anderson formed New Zealand&#8217;s first operator-run fund, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nzvc.co.nz\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">NZVC<\/a>, over the last year and made its first close of $10 million on what Pavlyukovskyy said will end up being around $15 million when all is said and done.<\/p>\n<p>Pavlyukovskyy, who was born in Ukraine and grew up in the United States, <a href=\"https:\/\/medium.com\/@pavlyukovskyy\/i-accidentally-ended-up-in-new-zealand-during-corona-heres-what-i-learned-442fe5fb967a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">came to New Zealand<\/a> as part of the Edmund Hillary Fellowship visa program just as the country closed the border during the global pandemic.<\/p>\n<p>He had previously exited edtech company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/09\/23\/piper-lets-kids-design-circuits-using-minecraft-and-electricity\/\">Piper<\/a> and was traveling around to other countries examining their education technology when he learned about New Zealand and the Hillary entrepreneur visa.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2279119\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cIn meeting and talking to founders, I saw interesting talent coming here, but there was no support, and startups were very undercapitalized and had low valuations,\u201d Pavlyukovskyy said. \u201cWe started talking about how we could leverage our connections to Silicon Valley to help New Zealand companies scale.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>He says when looking at the New Zealand startup ecosystem, it is similar to Israel and Singapore, and has \u201cfountains of talent.\u201d Despite being isolated geographically, it has a strong connection to the rest of the world. He likened the country&#8217;s culture to what you might see in the U.S. and Canada, it has a stable political system and, despite the remote location, has an entrepreneurial spirit.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2279989\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2279989\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2279989 size-large\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg?w=680\" alt=\"NZVC\" width=\"680\" height=\"384\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg 1024w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg?resize=150,85 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg?resize=768,434 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg?resize=680,384 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/WhatsApp-Image-2022-03-04-at-12.46.35-PM-e1646401171679.jpeg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2279989\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Mark Pavlyukovskyy, far left, and venture partner Rich Bodo, third from left.<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In addition, he saw a very nascent funding ecosystem that mainly consisted of angel investors and some venture investors, but none of them were operators nor had much experience actually building companies from zero to 1, Pavlyukovskyy added.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThere were no other experienced founders to guide them or give them advice on how to build companies,\u201d he said. \u201cInvestors were coming in and messing up the cap table or the board structure. We want to come in early to prevent some of these problems from taking place. From me being a serial entrepreneur, I want to be able to give suggestions and advice, which is the fun part.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>As such, NZVC\u2019s fund is targeting the seed to Series A gap. The firm has deployed $4 million into 25 companies so far. Its limited partners are also operators and are either connected to New Zealand or provide an opportunity to get exposure to companies they may not have otherwise seen.<\/p>\n<p>For example, the investor base includes AngelList founder Naval Ravikant, Foundry Group\u2019s\u00a0 Brad Feld and Ryan McIntyre, Disney COO Tom Staggs and Skype founder Jaan Tallinn.<\/p>\n<p>The firm is focused on B2B SaaS, deep tech, marketplaces and the web3 and cryptocurrency space. Now that the pandemic has proven that today\u2019s entrepreneurs can start companies anywhere and locate their team anywhere, that has enabled founders to hire remote teams and do sales outside of New Zealand, Pavlyukovskyy said.<\/p>\n<p>NZVC has invested in companies like Seachange, which is doing hydrofoiling and electric car ferries, and Pyper Vision, a fog-clearing drone for airports. It is also infused capital into companies in the mental health space, including Chnnl, a platform for healthcare workers to give confidential feedback; Sahha, an AI-based tool to analyze mental health passively without asking you questions; and oVRcome, a VR-based product aimed at curing phobias through exposure therapy.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe New Zealand government strongly supports and subsidizes university research, and as a result, some companies have done well and have had successes,\u201d Pavlyukovskyy added.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" Zealand","slug":"new-zealand","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/5833"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=5833"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=5833"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=5833"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=5833"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576990129,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/nzvc\/","name":"NZVC","slug":"nzvc","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576990129"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576990129"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576990129"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576990129"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576990129"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2279006,"date":"2022-03-03T06:00:54","date_gmt":"2022-03-03T14:00:54","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2279006"},"modified":"2022-03-02T12:07:23","modified_gmt":"2022-03-02T20:07:23","slug":"archive-community-marketing","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/03\/archive-community-marketing\/","title":{"rendered":"Archive back with fresh funding as it builds community marketing space"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Now that a lot of transactions take place in e-commerce, tapping into the community is something merchants are finding is a necessity to continue engaging with customers.<\/p>\n<p>However, that community can live in a bunch of different places online, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.archive.ai\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Archive<\/a> is working to harness that community, wherever it is, and provide insights on how the merchant can use that data to grow.<\/p>\n<p>We first caught up with company co-founders Paul Benigeri and Geoffrey Woo last November when the company announced a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/03\/archive-ai-aims-to-free-marketers-from-their-monotonous-workflows\/\">$4 million seed round<\/a> led by Stripe. At the time, Archive was going public with its technology aimed at connecting databases and distribution channels so they talk to each other.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2279006\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Its first products were a Shopify app that automatically detects, classifies and saves Instagram stories relating to a brand, and Archive Communities, which makes influencer marketing programmatic so that brands can more quickly scale their community-building efforts.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"YmtTslW4lZ\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/03\/archive-ai-aims-to-free-marketers-from-their-monotonous-workflows\/\">Archive.ai aims to free marketers from their monotonous workflows<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Archive.ai aims to free marketers from their monotonous workflows&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/03\/archive-ai-aims-to-free-marketers-from-their-monotonous-workflows\/embed\/#?secret=rwh8ON8sFs#?secret=YmtTslW4lZ\" data-secret=\"YmtTslW4lZ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2279015\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2279015\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2279015 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg\" alt=\"Archive\" width=\"1024\" height=\"580\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg 1410w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg?resize=150,85 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg?resize=300,170 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg?resize=768,435 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg?resize=680,385 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Team-Photo-Archive.jpeg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2279015\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Archive \/ Archive&#8217;s team<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Since coming out of beta with fewer than 50 customers, Archive closed January with more than 500 customers, and Woo told TechCrunch that the company\u2019s goal is to reach 1,000 by the end of the first quarter. Its app was also the No. 1 trending app on Spotify the first week it was launched.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe are the first Shopify app to do automatic archival and classification of Instagram stories,\u201d said Woo, who is the company\u2019s chairman. \u201cJust this simple tool has saved a lot of time for merchants, and from that angle, we become the primary interface with marketers to start their workflow.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Four months later, the company also attracted attention from Tiger Global and Human Capital, which co-led Archive\u2019s latest $8 million seed extension. Battery Ventures, Anti Fund, Red Antler and 305 Ventures also participated in the round, as did a group of individual investors, including Brex COO Michael Tannenbaum, Extend co-founder Rohan Shah and Alloy Automation CEO Sara Du.<\/p>\n<p>This gives Archive a $100 million post-money valuation and brings its total funding amount to $12 million since the company was founded in March 2021, Woo said.<\/p>\n<p>The company was not planning to raise so soon, given that it had just come out of stealth mode and was working to get the company\u2019s story out there, Woo said. However, with merchants struggling with customer acquisition, especially through platforms like Facebook, demand for help in this area grew quickly.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019ve always had interest given our background and speed of growth,\u201d Woo added. \u201cWe thought it was smart to build out our cap table with Tiger, Human Capital and angels. It is a healthy step up from the initial round led by Stripe and puts us in a strong position to invest in our technology and platform.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Woo plans to invest the new capital into tripling the technical team of engineers and designers. The company has nearly 10 full-time roles it is looking to fill and is also considering its first full-time marketer and business operation positions.<\/p>\n<p>Woo is a computer scientist by trade and says the company wants to build out the automation and pipes so that customers can focus more on their creative and messages that resonate with their consumers.<\/p>\n<p>It also rebranded to Archive.com and will start a content platform and acquire conferences and newsletters to be a first mover in terms of what the future of marketing should look like. And, as it continues to build out the category of community marketing, it is looking at new areas, like how the changing of privacy settings, web3 and cryptocurrency are affecting audiences.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cMarketing is not top-down anymore, it is bottom-up and all the software, processes and workflow don\u2019t exist for that new wave of marketing,\u201d Woo said. \u201cWe are helping provide the automation and software to power the next generation of marketing, which is community marketing.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Ng6YbPtvCI\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/23\/10-growth-marketing-experts-share-their-2022-predictions-and-new-years-resolutions\/\">10 growth marketing experts share their 2022 predictions and New Year&#8217;s resolutions<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" whips up new tools for independent restaurants following funding"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Six months after taking in its initial funding to provide independent restaurants with online ordering tools, <a href=\"http:\/\/owner.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Owner.com<\/a> is back with an expanded suite of offerings around delivery and marketing automation after securing $15 million in fresh funding.<\/p>\n<p>Aiming to manage a restaurant\u2019s entire digital presence, the company has relaunched itself to offer new tools for its users to do everything from create and update their websites, email marketing and leverage features like recruiting and reputation management, so that everything is in one place versus paying for dozens of subscriptions for each aspect.<\/p>\n<p>We first spoke with Owner.com\u2019s co-founder and CEO Adam Guild during the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/owner-com-serves-up-10-7m-so-that-independent-restaurants-can-get-cooking\/\">company\u2019s initial $10.7 million in funding<\/a> to talk about the company\u2019s early goals to become a \u201cShopify meets Salesforce\u201d offering for independent restaurants.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2279018\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>At the time, Owner.com had already reached a seven-figure run-rate and over 105% monthly revenue retention across more than 700 restaurant locations after finding its footing in a crowded space dominated by players like DoorDash, UberEats and GrubHub, which were charging between 20% and 30% on orders, a margin often too high for independent restaurants, which represent 40% of the U.S. restaurant industry.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gRsnYvKrsx\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/owner-com-serves-up-10-7m-so-that-independent-restaurants-can-get-cooking\/\">Owner.com serves up $10.7M so that independent restaurants can get cooking<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Owner.com serves up $10.7M so that independent restaurants can get cooking&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/owner-com-serves-up-10-7m-so-that-independent-restaurants-can-get-cooking\/embed\/#?secret=us00zmzapO#?secret=gRsnYvKrsx\" data-secret=\"gRsnYvKrsx\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe kept hearing from restaurants that they hated having to use 15 different tools to manage every piece of their digital presence,\u201d Guild told TechCrunch. \u201cThey told us that it was super expensive, time-consuming and clunky for their customers to have a different tool for every piece.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The Series A round was led by Altman Capital, with participation from Redpoint Ventures, Day One Ventures, SaaStr Fund, Browder Capital and a group of angel investors, including Instacart\u2019s Max Mullen, FTX\u2019s Sam Bankman-Fried,\u00a0 Rippling\u2019s Parker Conrad, Flexport\u2019s Ryan Petersen, Mercury\u2019s Immad Akhund and AgentSync\u2019s Niranjan Sabharwal. Additional existing investors include Kimbal Musk and Figma\u2019s Dylan Field. The company has now raised $26 million to date.<\/p>\n<p>Following its seed round, the company \u201cstill had tons of runway,\u201d and wasn\u2019t planning to raise additional funds for at least another year, said Guild, who started the company with Dean Bloembergen in 2020. However, after sending out the November investor update, the company received seven preemptive offers for its next round from what Guild said were \u201csome incredible investors.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe decided that it was better to save ourselves time in the future by accepting the money early from some incredible people,\u201d Guild added.<\/p>\n<p>Guild explained that the company chose to deepen its relationship with Altman Capital, and as part of the investment, Jack Altman is joining Owner.com\u2019s board, a person Guild said was a \u201cdream board member.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2279027\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2279027\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2279027\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1E3BAB03-A46E-428A-9644-A3E398136E78.jpg\" alt=\"Owner.com\" width=\"1024\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/1E3BAB03-A46E-428A-9644-A3E398136E78.jpg 4000w, class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Owner.com<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere is a very important movement happening where restaurant owners are finally being given a platform to take back control from big corporations, and Owner.com is paving the way for mom-and-pop shops to succeed,\u201d Altman said via a written statement.<\/p>\n<p>Since its last round, Guild said the company is growing at over 20% month over month, and revealed that the new funding values Owner.com at $150 million. It is on track to grow its annual recurring revenue by more than 700% in 2022. It is also now in 49 states and working with more than 1,500 restaurants.<\/p>\n<p>The new capital will enable the company to add to its employee headcount and invest in product development, including adding reservations and catering products, so that Owner.com can, in Guild\u2019s words, \u201cdisrupt the tyranny of OpenTable and EzCater and build our communications platform for restaurants to use to manage all of their digital communications in one place.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, the restaurant tech market is becoming a crowded space as startups step in to help restaurants embrace the digital age. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.marketwatch.com\/press-release\/at-1489-cagr-restaurant-management-software-market-size-will-reach-695-billion-usd-by-2025-2022-01-19\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Market Study Report<\/a> predicts the global restaurant management software market to grow nearly 15% annually to reach $6.95 billion by 2025. Owner.com is also joining a long list of funding announcements we\u2019ve seen in just the past few months; for example, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/11\/agot-ai-gives-restaurants-computer-vision-to-see-where-food-orders-go-wrong\/\">Agot AI<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/01\/coatue-lunchbox-ghost-kitchen-restaurant-tech\/\">Lunchbox<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/24\/deliverect-raises-150m-at-a-1-4b-valuation-to-streamline-online-and-offline-food-orders\/\">Deliverect<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/17\/nigerian-restaurant-management-platform-orda-gets-1-1m-wants-to-be-the-toast-of-africa\/\">Orda<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/10\/digital-restaurant-startup-zak-orders-up-new-capital-on-mission-to-be-toast-of-latam\/\">Zak<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/22\/sunday-raises-100-million-for-its-fast-restaurant-checkout-flow\/\">Sunday<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/13\/marginedge-a-restaurant-management-software-company-raises-18m\/\">Margin Edge<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Despite all of that new technology, Guild explained that it\u2019s \u201ctoo complicated and expensive for independent restaurants to have a point solution for every piece of their online presence,\u201d which could end up being hundreds of piecemeal tools needed to manage a restaurant\u2019s digital presence.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cUsing them takes more time and money than restaurant owners have,\u201d he added. \u201cWe already save our owners an average of seven hours a month, plus over $2,750 a month in fees, and automate all of the things that they would otherwise have to do manually in synchronizing data across their existing tools.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><em>Editor&#8217;s note: 8:02 a.m. PST, added the company&#8217;s valuation<\/em>.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" management","slug":"reputation-management","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/304022"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=304022"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=304022"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=304022"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=304022"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2278362,"date":"2022-03-02T06:00:59","date_gmt":"2022-03-02T14:00:59","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2278362"},"modified":"2022-03-01T15:26:19","modified_gmt":"2022-03-01T23:26:19","slug":"99minutos-logistics-infrastructure-latin-america","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/99minutos-logistics-infrastructure-latin-america\/","title":{"rendered":"99minutos clocks in fresh capital for logistics infrastructure in Latin America"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">99minutos, a logistics service company for e-commerce vendors across Latin America, is making fast work out of attracting funding. It announced today $82 million in Series C funding, led by Oak HC\/FT, with participation from existing investors Kaszek and Prosus Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>The last round follows a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/99-minutos-mexicos-last-mile-delivery-startup-raises-a-40m-series-b\/\">$40 million Series B investment<\/a> last May from Prosus and Kaszek and brings the company\u2019s total funding to about $128.7 million. It was then that we learned about the origins of the Mexico City-based company, founded by CEO Alexis Patjane, who had been running a food truck-making business in Mexico.<\/p>\n<p>Patjane told TechCrunch that he wasn\u2019t immediately looking for additional capital after closing the Series B, and in fact had plans to begin raising again this year. However, opportunities with new customers came along, the company was growing and there was a ton of interest from venture capital firms.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2278362\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cThat interest didn\u2019t happen before,\u201d he added. \u201cIt has been a life-changing round. We contacted 77 funds, and three said \u2018yes,\u2019 and the rest said \u2018no.\u2019 It was depressing to hear all of the \u2018nos.\u2019 Now that we have positioned the brand and the company, getting interest from the other side is flattering, and helps to make things move faster.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PRk3Nv9bL5\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/99-minutos-mexicos-last-mile-delivery-startup-raises-a-40m-series-b\/\">99 minutos, Mexico&#8217;s last mile delivery startup, raises a $40M Series B<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;99 minutos, Mexico&#8217;s last mile delivery startup, raises a $40M Series B&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/07\/99-minutos-mexicos-last-mile-delivery-startup-raises-a-40m-series-b\/embed\/#?secret=ppUS9Lq3aa#?secret=PRk3Nv9bL5\" data-secret=\"PRk3Nv9bL5\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>He particularly was interested in speaking with Oak HC\/FT because of its global presence and approach to bringing together its portfolio companies around tips and advice for founders. Patjane didn\u2019t divulge 99minutos\u2019 valuation, but did say the company is now shy of being a unicorn, and in the next round, he would be able to announce something bigger.<\/p>\n<p>Since e-commerce and logistics companies, like Amazon, came to Mexico, there has been much infrastructure created around this industry, Patjane said. Traditional companies, like FedEx and DHL were there before, as were country-specific delivery companies, but the service was costly, not available every day and wasn\u2019t tied to technology.<\/p>\n<p>As the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.statista.com\/statistics\/445860\/retail-e-commerce-sales-latam\/#:~:text=In%202020%2C%20retail%20e%2Dcommerce,160%20billion%20dollars%20by%202025\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">retail e-commerce market in Latin America<\/a> is poised to reach $160 million by 2025, compared with an estimated $85 billion in 2021, Patjane believes 99minutos needs to be the first technology company to build the logistics infrastructure required to scale, to have a fast delivery experience \u2014 getting packages tomorrow instead of 10 days from now \u2014 and offer specialized services.<\/p>\n<p>When we last reported on the company in 2021, it was operating in 40 markets and is now in 60 markets across Mexico, Colombia, Chile and Peru, with a goal of opening in two more countries, yet to be determined, this year. Patjane plans to be at 95% penetration in all of its current markets before connecting services to other countries.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Meanwhile, the company is handling over 15 million packages per year, with a goal of delivering them in less than 99 minutes, same-day or next-day via its fleet of electric vehicles.<\/p>\n<p>Patjane intends to invest the new funding into scaling new business models, expanding into new geographic areas with Latin America and new sustainability initiatives in line with the company\u2019s low-carbon goals of increasing its use of electric vehicles.<\/p>\n<p>Some of its new offerings since the last raise include Punto 99, a pick-up and drop-off network that addresses the entire fulfillment process and returns. The company opened more than 500 stations, which include printing stations for labels, where people can pick up or drop off their packages. Patjane expects to increase the number of those \u201chubs\u201d to 8,000 in Mexico by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>It also has a route tracking and optimization SaaS tool for customers called Routa 99 that figures out the best way to get a package to its destination and in what kind of vehicle.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, 99minutos has 5,000 employees working from Mexico, Colombia, Chile and Peru, and Patjane aims to reach between 8,000 and 10,000 by the end of the year. It is also working with over 120,000 customers, mainly business-to-business companies. Revenue grew three times year over year.<\/p>\n<p>Allen Miller, principal at Oak HC\/FT, said in a written statement that the growth experienced in Latin America\u2019s e-commerce industry of the past few years has facilitated a need for better technology so that orders make it to their final destination.<\/p>\n<p>\u201c99minutos is meeting this need and has impressively expanded beyond its core last-mile offering to become the leading technology logistics and fulfillment company in the region,\u201d Miller added. \u201cWe look forward to supporting the team as the company continues its growth and expansion in LatAm.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"w5Q46UHSIZ\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/22\/last-mile-delivery-in-latin-america-is-ready-to-take-off\/\">Last-mile delivery in Latin America is ready to take off<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Last-mile delivery in Latin America is ready to take off&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/22\/last-mile-delivery-in-latin-america-is-ready-to-take-off\/embed\/#?secret=ihqnRflblJ#?secret=w5Q46UHSIZ\" data-secret=\"w5Q46UHSIZ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>99minutos, a logistics service company for e-commerce vendors across Latin America, is making fast work out of attracting funding. It announced today $82 million in Series C funding, led by Oak HC\/FT, with participation from existing investors Kaszek and Prosus Ventures. The last round follows a $40 million Series B investment last May from Prosus tc_video?tags=8590"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":215454,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/fedex\/","name":"fedex","slug":"fedex","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/215454"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=215454"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=215454"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=215454"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=215454"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2278195,"date":"2022-03-02T05:00:28","date_gmt":"2022-03-02T13:00:28","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2278195"},"modified":"2022-03-02T06:14:54","modified_gmt":"2022-03-02T14:14:54","slug":"enterpret-launches-with-4-4m-nlp-technology-to-decipher-customer-feedback","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/enterpret-launches-with-4-4m-nlp-technology-to-decipher-customer-feedback\/","title":{"rendered":"Enterpret launches with $4.3M, NLP technology to decipher customer feedback"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Advances in natural language processing are making it possible for companies to gather and learn from customers in new and better ways to help product development teams with their product roadmaps.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.enterpret.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Enterpret<\/a> is emerging onto the scene with its take on building analytics on natural language so that people building the product can learn directly from customer feedback without relying on another company department to provide the information.<\/p>\n<p>The company was co-founded in June 2020 by Varun Sharma, who previously worked at LinkedIn and in customer success for Amplitude, and his brother, Arnav Sharma, who did research on NLP at Uber.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2278195\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The desire to learn from customer feedback has always existed, but the way companies do it has changed over time, Varun Sharma told TechCrunch. It used to be done via paper surveys that were mailed out, and you had to wait to get them back. Today, every interaction is digital.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe number of channels that companies interact with customers has expanded to include apps, social media, in-app chat services and the new hot thing of community, like Discord and Slack,\u201d he added. \u201cThe people building the products want to know what people like and don\u2019t like, get the curated feedback, but never actually learn from customer feedback. That\u2019s very hard to quantify because it is not a direct query or feedback.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Enterpret is building and deploying customer-specific models, based on customer feedback, for product development teams. By starting with the machine learning approach for the custom models, Varun Sharma believes there is a higher recall of insights that companies using generic models are not able to produce.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2278201\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2278201\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2278201\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg\" alt=\"Enterpret, Varun Sharma, Arnav Sharma\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg 6000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Varun-Arnav-Sharma-2.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2278201\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Enterpret co-founders Varun Sharma and Arnav Sharma. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Enterpret<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>He is seeing a few use cases trickle to the top, including using Enterpret to plan what products or integrations to build, comparing feedback among users in a certain month to detect early signals that might have prevented churn and to run growth experiments to validate a product hypothesis.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to its launch, the company announced it raised $4.3 million in seed funding led by Kleiner Perkins, Sequoia Capital India and Unusual Ventures and included a group of angel investors.<\/p>\n<p>The driver for funding and taking the product out of beta was seeing early traction and positive return on investment from early partners, Varun Sharma said.<\/p>\n<p>Investors agree, with Josh Coyne, partner at Kleiner Perkins saying, &#8220;Enterpret has unlocked an entirely new way to distill customer voices to inform product development. Varun, Arnav, and the entire team have a unique vision and an impressive product velocity. We&#8217;re thrilled to be part of their journey.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The Sharmas plan to deploy the new funding into building out a team \u2014 it has gone from two to 15 employees already \u2014 in areas like R&amp;D, product development and go-to-market.<\/p>\n<p>Since the company has been in R&amp;D mode for the past few years, Varun Sharma was not yet ready to discuss revenue, but did say its handful of customers have been with them for many months, and he feels confident now to repeat the process across the world.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe will continue to develop a new way of customer intelligence,\u201d he added. \u201cWe are building workflows and processes so the right customer feedback reaches the right person at the right time.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"dFRD3goTiI\"><p><a feedback loops in the search for product-market fit<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; some of the world\u2019s biggest food companies develop new products, they go to Tastewise first"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Knowing the right time to bring a food product to market is traditionally handled through surveys and focus groups, but <a href=\"https:\/\/tastewise.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Tastewise<\/a> thinks this can be done better with technology.<\/p>\n<p>The Israeli-based company developed artificial intelligence-driven data analytics that help food brands make smarter decisions around product development, marketing and retail sales for their next healthy, sustainable and delicious product. It also monitors more than 1 million restaurants across the world and connects food brands with those eager to try their foods.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s been able to rack up a customer base of some of the top food and beverage companies and up-and-coming food tech startups over the past five years, like Nestl\u00e9, PepsiCo, Kraft Heinz, Campbell\u2019s and JustEgg.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2278187\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>And now it has secured another round of funding, this time $17 million in Series A funding. Disruptive led the round and joined existing investors PeakBridge and PICO Venture Partners. The latest funding round gives Tastewise $21.5 million in total funding to date.<\/p>\n<p>Alon Chen, co-founder and CEO of Tastewise, is a self-taught engineer who started writing code when he was 12 and left a career at Google five years ago after getting the idea for the company from his mother\u2019s Shabbat dinner.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cMy mom makes a great Shabbat dinner, but she started asking us for our dietary needs for that week,\u201d he said. \u201cWith my co-founder (Eyal Gaon), we realized that consumers are changing dietary needs so much faster than before. It is the 21st century, and we still see 90% of the 30,000 new products that launch each year fail. A one-size-fits-all approach is no longer possible.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>He explained that even the most innovative food tech companies still rely on outdated retail data to come up with their product strategies, and if you don\u2019t come with the right data, you will get the wrong answer.<\/p>\n<p>So Chen and Gaon set out to build a platform dedicated to data so that food and beverage companies can disrupt the $10 trillion industry with healthier foods, new flavors and plant-based varieties, and do it in a way that accelerates sales and acceptance of new products.<\/p>\n<p>Since the company started in 2017, Chen says Tastewise has been operating lean, previously raising capital in both 2020 and 2021. The company tripled revenue between 2020 and 2021 and is now working to expand its data and workforce beyond the United States and United Kingdom to India, Australia, Germany, Canada and France.<\/p>\n<p>It already doubled its employee count in the U.S. and Israel and is working with nearly 15% of the top 100 food and beverage brands and dozens of food tech startups.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhen we first started Tastewise, food tech was not there yet, and when we started talking to investors about doing predictive analytics for food and beverage, we told them this is the future,\u201d Chen said. \u201cWe have to help the world get data, improve the food industry and make it more healthy and delicious.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote Venture Partners","slug":"pico-venture-partners","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576666356"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576666356"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576666356"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576666356"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576666356"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2277593,"date":"2022-03-01T06:00:25","date_gmt":"2022-03-01T14:00:25","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2277593"},"modified":"2022-03-01T08:05:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-01T16:05:57","slug":"riogrande-takes-in-first-capital-to-incubate-latin-americas-next-local-brands","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/riogrande-takes-in-first-capital-to-incubate-latin-americas-next-local-brands\/","title":{"rendered":"Riogrande takes in first capital to incubate Latin America\u2019s next local brands"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Tono Mandly doesn\u2019t consider his company, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.riogrande.co\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Riogrande<\/a>, an e-commerce aggregator, but instead as one whose mission is to build local brands, through acquisition and incubation, for the emerging middle class of Latin American consumers.<\/p>\n<p>Latin America continues to be one of the fastest growing e-commerce markets in the world, with $100 billion in total addressable market, he pointed out. However, it remains a highly fragmented market where only the wealthiest consumers have the ability to purchase goods from the U.S., while half a billion people in the middle and lower classes have to turn to China for cheaper, often lower-quality products, Mandly added.<\/p>\n<p>He, Federico Naides and Ivan Amelong started the company in Mexico City in 2021 to close that disparity by incubating brands and acquiring small and medium brands selling on marketplaces like MercadoLibre and Amazon. They come from backgrounds that include Rocket Internet and Delivery Hero.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2277593\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe are building great local brands for the middle class and lower class, mainly creating new brands from zero, but also doing some acquisitions where we can multiply the brand by 30 times,\u201d Mandly added. \u201cUnlike aggregators, of which there are a couple in LatAm bringing a few brands together with multiple arbitrage, we are focused on the growth play and how to automate the process of growth so that the companies see growth in a month that others see in a year.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>While e-commerce aggregators have emerged all over the world, it is a fairly new concept in Latin America, but experiencing explosive growth, driven in part by the global pandemic\u2019s impact on e-commerce. Many are seeing success, for example, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/09\/e-commerce-aggregator-merama-gets-its-horn-after-just-12-months-in-business\/\">Merama<\/a>, which hit a $1.2 billion valuation just 12 months after incorporation, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/08\/quinio-jumps-into-world-of-e-commerce-aggregators-with-20m-seed\/\">Quinio<\/a>, which announced $20 million in initial funding to acquire some 30 companies, and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/12\/wonder-brands-picks-up-20m-aims-to-build-marketplace-of-latin-american-e-commerce-brands\/\">Wonder Brands<\/a>, which also picked up $20 million.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Unlike the aggregators, which Mandly explained aim to acquire hundreds of brands, Riogrande is going for something more intimate, maybe 30 brands doing $30 million in revenue per year. It will acquire about half of those and create the other half.<\/p>\n<p>Riogrande focuses on brands like home, kitchen and beauty, and after going through Y Combinator, has already taken several brands in the home space from zero to $1 million in revenue in a span of two months.<\/p>\n<p>To help the company scale its plan, it took in $12 million in seeding funding in a round led by Y Combinator and Wollef, with participation from individual investors including Arielle Zuckerberg and Justin Mateen.<\/p>\n<p>Mandly said some of the funding has already been deployed into technology development, so Riogrande can automate every process of brand growth and supply chain and do a few more acquisitions. He expects to also close on a Series A round in the coming weeks.<\/p>\n<p>In the past year, the company doubled its revenue with a goal of reaching $1 billion in topline with 35% EBITDA margins. Riogrande is already profitable, and Mandly says it can now shift comfortably between growth and profitability.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe have our heads down to work, keep growing and maintain the growth rates with our brands,\u201d he added. \u201cFounders are looking for us because there are no other players who have our growth rates.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote fintechs are laying down new global commerce rails<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: near an ocean? Kin Insurance\u2019s data aims to more accurately predict home risk"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A home in California has different insurance needs than a home in Nebraska, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kin.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Kin Insurance<\/a> believes data and technology can determine the best way to insure homes where insurance is harder to get.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s been a few years since we caught up with the Chicago-based direct-to-consumer home insurance company after it <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/08\/01\/kin-insurance\/\">raised $4 million<\/a>, but CEO Sean Harper told TechCrunch that among the $110 billion home insurance market, half of the homes are in regions exposed to extreme weather and fires.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere is a lot of demand for insurance because people are increasingly moving to those places,\u201d he added. \u201cThere are some places in the U.S. where you shouldn\u2019t live, like on a barrier island or in historic flood planes. However, if you choose to live there, insurance is expensive. Using a special sauce of the technology, we are good at understanding that a county is big, and you shouldn\u2019t be painting every home with the same brush.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2277577\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Harper, who co-founded the company with Lucas Ward,\u00a0Jason Heidkamp\u00a0and\u00a0Sebastian Villarreal, explained that legacy insurance companies don\u2019t have the data needed to determine which homes are risky and which ones are not, so they often end up making a leap at pricing, resulting in higher underwriting.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Jk1Rhv2iav\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/08\/01\/kin-insurance\/\">With $4 million in funding, Kin wants to change how homeowners get insured<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;With $4 million in funding, Kin wants to change how homeowners get insured&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/08\/01\/kin-insurance\/embed\/#?secret=0JMCAoxUYs#?secret=Jk1Rhv2iav\" data-secret=\"Jk1Rhv2iav\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Instead, by using data to accurately price the risk, Kin Insurance may not always be the lowest price, but on average, ends up being cheaper because the company is better at segmenting the risk and using technology to take some of the costs out of it, like agents. He estimates selling insurance through agents costs 20% of the total premium on an ongoing basis.<\/p>\n<p>Harper also says it made sense 50 years ago to have local agents, but technology is so that insurance companies can not go directly to the consumer and still offer similar customer service via email, text, chat or telephone.<\/p>\n<p>After raising $80 million in Series C funding last April, Kin Insurance was poised to merge with Omnichannel Acquisition Corp., a special purpose acquisition company, to go public. However, in January, the company <a href=\"https:\/\/www.insurancebusinessmag.com\/us\/news\/technology\/ceo-turns-back-to-private-markets-after-reverse-merger-derailment-324535.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">decided not to move ahead with the deal<\/a>, Harper said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cPart of it was that the public market conditions were not great,\u201d he added. \u201cWe went all the way through the SEC process, but weren&#8217;t seeing the kind of market for tech companies that was there a year ago. There will be a time in the future when the market is good for tech companies again, and Kin will go public.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As the company was deciding whether to remain private, venture capital firms were lining up in case it didn\u2019t.<\/p>\n<p>Today, the company announced it raised $82 million of a Series D round that Harper expects will officially close at $100 million. QED Investors led the round and was joined by existing investors Commerce Ventures, Flourish Ventures, Hudson Structured Capital Management Ltd. (HSCM Bermuda), Alpha Edison, Allegis NL Capital, Avanta Ventures and August Capital, and new investors Geodesic Capital and PROOF.VC. Previously, the company raised $133 million in equity funding and $50 million in debt, Harper confirmed.<\/p>\n<p>Kin Insurance is among its <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/20\/insurtech-startups-are-leveraging-rapid-growth-to-raise-big-money\/\">insurtech peers experiencing rapid growth<\/a>, and in its case, closed 2021 with $105 million in premiums, up from $25 million in 2020, and with it, attracting new capital. Harper expects that growth trajectory to continue this year with the company on a path to close on more than $250 million in premiums in 2022.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to growing its premiums over the past year, the company grew its employee headcount to 450 from 250 at the beginning of 2021.<\/p>\n<p>The company is already operating in Florida, Louisiana and California, which Harper says is an almost $25 billion insurance market with just those three states, and the new funding will enable the company to move into half a dozen more states this year. Kin Insurance will also focus on investment in marketing, data science and technology.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cMore data about claims makes underwriting pricing more accurate,\u201d Harper added. \u201cThat is the big difference in how we do our underwriting versus the legacy companies, and we want to make that gap wider.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7Dar1yp6Cg\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/20\/insurtech-startups-are-leveraging-rapid-growth-to-raise-big-money\/\">Insurtech startups are leveraging rapid growth to raise big money<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Insurtech startups are leveraging rapid growth to raise big money&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/20\/insurtech-startups-are-leveraging-rapid-growth-to-raise-big-money\/embed\/#?secret=3jlC1V4OAa#?secret=7Dar1yp6Cg\" data-secret=\"7Dar1yp6Cg\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>By using data and technology to accurately price the risk, Kin Insurance is able to remove some of the costs of traditional insurance firms, like agents.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"author":133574474,"featured_media":2277840,"comment_status":"open","ping_status":"closed","sticky":false,"template":"","format":"standard","meta":{"outcome":"","status":"","crunchbase_tag":0,"amp_status":"","relegenceEntities":[],"relegenceSubjects":[],"carmot_uuid":"5e3b14a6-b148-3e7b-a067-c100002979ea"},"categories":[424613844,576602978,60523764,576602979,576605952,20429,17396],"tags":[5719083,104520593,576638748,427049652,576855833,12498,448128451,576989378,576989375,576989377,48861415,576989376,576989379,449557042,576606687,3857655],"crunchbase_tag":[],"tc_stories_tax":[],"tc_ec_category":[],"tc_event":[],"jetpack_featured_media_url":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/lucas-and-sean.jpg","parsely":{"version":"1.0.0","meta":{"@context":"http:\/\/schema.org","@type":"NewsArticle","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/live-near-an-ocean-kin-insurances-data-aims-to-more-accurately-predict-home-risk\/"},"headline":"Live near an ocean? helps brands sell products, at the point of discovery, with one click"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">We\u2019ve all seen a product on social media that looks interesting, so you click the \u201cshop now\u201d button and are taken over to a new site. But wait, you weren\u2019t finished on the social media site, and when you go back, everything has refreshed.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.ownit.co\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ownit<\/a> unveiled a checkout experience today, after testing with 10 companies, that gives direct-to-consumer brands a way to sell their products without that interruption. Its technology connects social, commerce and payment options at the point of discovery so consumers can buy in one tap via an \u201cOwnit Connected Checkout link.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>From the link, consumers go to a web page interface on top of the app and can make purchase choices from their favorite commerce site, including Shopify and Amazon, and pay with Apple Pay, Google Pay, Shop Pay or PayPal \u2014 features not often available because some social media sites don\u2019t often play well with certain payment options, Ownit co-founder and CEO Payman Nejati told TechCrunch.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2277010\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Nejati started San Francisco-based Ownit less than a year ago with Evan Shiue and Joel Tan, and all three have vast experience in checkout. This is Nejati\u2019s fifth startup, and most of his experience is in grocery checkout, while Shiue has a background in autonomous checkout at Standard Cognition and Walmart, and Tan in conversational checkout with Amazon\u2019s Alexa.<\/p>\n<p>The global pandemic was the driver for many people to start an e-commerce brand, and while many tools enable them to start easily, Nejati says the right tools haven\u2019t been there to help those companies grow as easily. In addition, brands still deal with challenges, like cart abandonment rates of 75%.<\/p>\n<p>Needless to say, they\u2019ve thought a lot about what\u2019s going on at the point of purchase, even going so far as to boast that customers will double sales conversion or pay nothing. They knew they were on to something as they saw checkout companies like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/14\/online-checkout-bolt-decacorn\/\">Bolt<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/12\/checkout-com-raises-1b-round-at-40b-valuation\/\">Checkout.com<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/rapyd-raises-300m-on-a-2-5b-valuation-to-boost-its-fintech-as-a-service-api\/\">Rapyd<\/a> collectively raising over $3 billion investments in the past 18 months.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2277020\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2277020\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2277020\" https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/2-Mid-Article-Image-Ownit-Founding-Team.jpg?resize=1536,960 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/2-Mid-Article-Image-Ownit-Founding-Team.jpg?resize=2048,1280 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/2-Mid-Article-Image-Ownit-Founding-Team.jpg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2277020\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Ownit<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe knew checkouts at the point of purchase will explode, but we wonder if the user was going to the storefront, and is the company investing in sending them there from another platform, like social media,\u201d Nejati added. \u201cAt the same time, the new iOS was making those costs unbearable. So we thought, what if you don\u2019t have to go there, but we could capture someone at the point of discovery \u2014 that was the lightbulb moment.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Proving that checkout continues to be a hot area for investors, Ownit itself announced initial funding Monday, an $8 million seed round from Caffeinated Capital, SciFi VC, GGV Capital, Abstract Ventures and a group of angel investors that include founders and executives of companies including Meta, Pinterest, Honey, Product Hunt, Standard Cognition and Anycart.<\/p>\n<p>Nejati explained Ownit is like the \u201cPlaid of e-commerce;\u201d what it is doing is a \u201cheavy tech lift,\u201d involving connecting people, merchants and payment options seamlessly. The ultimate goal being to become the merchant of record by going after capital to get everything squared away correctly from the beginning versus taking shortcuts that make it difficult to scale.<\/p>\n<p>As such, the new capital will be deployed into what Shiue called \u201cthe three Cs\u201d: conversion, which he considers \u201cthe North Star for its brands;\u201d customer onboarding; and connections to deepen the three pillars of its tool suite of social, commerce and payment platform relationships.<\/p>\n<p>The company has 11 employees currently and Shiue expects to be at 30 by the end of the year.<\/p>\n<p>Among Ownit\u2019s 10 early beta customers are consumer packaged goods companies, cosmetics and nutrition. Customers were encouraged to test sales through Shopify versus through Ownit, and Shiue said initial results have been positive, showing campaigns saw an average of two times the conversion lift via text marketing and three times conversion via email marketing.<\/p>\n<p>Up next, Nejati and Shiue say they still have some catching up to do in the market as they work to build out this brand new space in checkout.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"oADmt1Qe3K\"><p><a delivers second big funding round in a year, this time backed by SoftBank"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Coming off of a year where monthly active users grew 150% year over year, multicultural e-grocer <a href=\"https:\/\/www.sayweee.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Weee!<\/a> secured $425 million in Series E funding toward its goal to be \u201cthe primary source for food at home,\u201d Larry Liu, Weee!\u2019s founder and CEO, told me.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s been a few years since we <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/17\/weee-35-million-raise-from-dst\/\">dug into what the company was doing<\/a>, but to bring you up to speed, it was founded in 2015 and offers over 10,000 locally sourced and hard-to-find Chinese, Japanese, Korean, Vietnamese, Filipino, Indian and Latin offerings for customers.<\/p>\n<p>One of Liu\u2019s missions is product assortment, so Weee! typically adds more than 500 new products per week. It also partners with over 1,000 restaurants to offer authentic food-at-home options for customers, many as a result of the company\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/ethnic-e-grocer-weee-announces-acquisition-of-online-asian-food-delivery-company-ricepo-301405492.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquisition of RICEPO<\/a>, an Asian food delivery company, in October.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2277116\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>This new monster round not only comes about a year after the company\u2019s $316 million Series D round last March, but boosts Weee!\u2019s valuation to $4.1 billion. It also nearly doubles the company\u2019s total fundraising, bringing it to over $800 million to date, Liu said.<\/p>\n<p>Taking in the new capital was an intentional move for Liu, who wants to grow the business to the next level. While it has made progress, he wants to deepen Weee!\u2019s supply chain, focus on building relationships with vendors, do more direct importing of products to the U.S. and expand into two more ethnicities.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe have a really powerful and unique value proposition in targeting underserved communities and want to offer the most amazing assortment for the community,\u201d he added. \u201cThat is our biggest differentiation, and that strategy is working well for us.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In addition, the company will also advance its warehouse automation and artificial intelligence technology to offer the most relevant product recommendations.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Weee! Currently has about 1,500 employees and will continue to build out a team to scale, including on the go-to-market side, where Liu said the company had not invested heavily before, saying, \u201cWe are a best-kept secret, and a lot of people didn\u2019t know about us, but we want to make sure people know what we are doing.\u201d The company this month <a href=\"https:\/\/www.winsightgrocerybusiness.com\/retailers\/online-grocer-weee-adds-filmmaker-jon-chu-creative-chief\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">hired filmmaker Jon Chu as chief creative officer<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>SoftBank Vision Fund 2 led the financing and was joined by Greyhound Capital. As part of the investment, Lydia Jett, managing partner at SoftBank Investment Advisers, will join Weee!\u2019s board of directors.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe market for ethnic groceries and food is massively underserved in the U.S. and we believe that Weee! is in a prime position to meet the demands of customers,\u201d Jett said in a written statement. \u201cWeee!\u2019s strong execution capabilities and reach across multiple ethnic groups, coupled with a unique customer experience model leveraging AI, has enabled it to scale effectively in a rapidly evolving grocery market.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>For Liu, product assortment and pricing are most important. He is looking to expand into household and beauty items so that Weee! can transition into more of a mainstream store versus only ethnic items.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe believe convenience is important, too, but that doesn\u2019t mean you have to get items in 30 minutes,\u201d he added. \u201cWe are focused on bringing people affordable access to the products they love and see the future being a store where we can offer a wide variety of products.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"pg7O3sD6lf\"><p><a Dairy slices into new funding for animal-free cheeses"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Food tech company <a href=\"https:\/\/betterdairy.co.uk\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Better Dairy<\/a> is closer to getting its aged and hard cheeses into the testing phase after securing $22 million in Series A funding.<\/p>\n<p>The U.K.-based company, founded in 2019 by Jevan Nagarajah, is still in the R&amp;D phase of developing animal-free cheeses using precision fermentation. We initially got to know Nagarajah and Better Dairy back in 2020 when the company raised <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/17\/better-dairy\/\">\u00a31.6 million in seed funding<\/a> in a round led by Happiness Capital.<\/p>\n<p>At the time, he explained that animal-based dairy farming was \u201chugely unsustainable,\u201d needing 650 liters of water to produce just 1 liter of milk and utilizing a process that emits the equivalent of over 1.7 billion tonnes of CO<sub>2<\/sub> into the atmosphere each year.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2277125\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Instead, Better Dairy is using precision fermentation to produce products that are molecularly identical to traditional dairy, Nagarajah said. The process is similar to brewing beer, with the end result being dairy.<\/p>\n<p>While other food tech companies are tackling softer cheeses like mozzarella or whey proteins, Better Daily is targeting hard cheeses, a process that is more complex, in a more sustainable way.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2277126\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2277126\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2277126\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg\" alt=\"Better Dairy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg 4771w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/Team-PIc.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2277126\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Better Dairy<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe see limitations in hard cheese, similar to trying to create animal-free steak,\u201d Nagarajah added. \u201cBy building a team that includes a chief scientific officer with 30 years of expertise making proteins for the pharmaceutical industry, we realized we could go complex and do it consciously.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Happiness Capital is back for the Series A, this time as a participant to the co-lead of RedAlpine and Vorwerk Ventures. Joining them are Manta Ray, Acequia Capital and Stray Dog Capital.<\/p>\n<p>Better Dairy is not alone in going after the dairy space. Companies like <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/07\/the-every-co-grabs-175m-as-it-cracks-code-on-animal-free-protein-products\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/url?q=https:\/\/theeverycompany.com\/&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1646238763622000&amp;usg=AOvVaw3xQLS2hcgi1enw58IHE5IP\">The EVERY Company <\/a>(formerly Clara Foods), <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/09\/competing-with-both-perfect-day-and-beyond-meat-chiles-notco-raises-85-million-to-expand-to-the-us\/\">NotCo<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/01\/founded-by-an-impossible-foods-and-google-data-scientist-climax-foods-raises-7-5-million-to-tackle-the-cheesiest-market\/\">Climax Foods<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/the-weeks-biggest-funding-rounds-faux-cheese-hunting-tech-talent-and-insurance-against-hackers\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Perfect Day<\/a> are all working on animal-alternative cheese and dairy products. However, Nagarajah believes that the new funding, aimed at advancing the precision fermentation technology, will help the company get out ahead of the competition to become the first player to launch hard cheeses in this space.<\/p>\n<p>The company is investing the capital into expanding its workforce from eight people to 35 and into a new 6,000-square-foot laboratory and office space in East London.<\/p>\n<p>Better Dairy is working on the science to nail down texture and then maturation so that all of the components can come together under one product that has a shelf life. Nagarajah is optimistic that the precision fermentation will get to unit economics \u2014 a.k.a. price parity with similar artisanal cheeses \u2014 in the next 18 months or so.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe need the right space and equipment to upgrade our science,\u201d he added. \u201cIt is not just about being animal-free and sustainable, but also delicious. If it tastes better then it becomes a no-brainer and a benchmark for success. There is a benefit for doing it the right way because if not, the time it takes to unwind it all could take years.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\"
