sweetens the process for e-commerce companies to take orders immediately"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Two years ago, entrepreneur Derek Low lost his hotel in Bali and began selling homemade cheesecakes online to make ends meet. However, he found it difficult to find an easy e-commerce tool that enabled him to quickly get up and running to take orders.<\/p>\n<p>Low noticed that 200 million businesses rely on the phone or messaging apps, like WhatsApp or Instagram, to take orders, a hard-to-track process that made it tough to collect payments. He also saw that a professional e-commerce website takes weeks to set up and is costly for new businesses.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2276398\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2276398\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-2276398\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"Cococart, Derek Low\" width=\"300\" height=\"215\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg 1280w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg?resize=150,107 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg?resize=300,215 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg?resize=768,550 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg?resize=680,487 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/derek.jpg?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2276398\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Derek Low, co-founder and CEO, Cococart. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cococart<\/p><\/div><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2276334\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Pairing up with Zhicong Lim, they founded the Singapore-based<a href=\"https:\/\/www.cococart.co\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> Cococart<\/a>, a tool to enable merchants to set up an online store in minutes with no code, no design and no app downloads. The store comes with everything from order management to mobile payment solutions. Merchants can manage their own sales without apps or marketplaces that charge unsustainable fees and commissions, Low added.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cHonestly, managing orders is hard,\u201d he said. \u201cMost local businesses are still taking orders on WhatsApp and managing their orders using spreadsheets. It sucks up so many hours of time, which could be better spent growing the business. We&#8217;re at the forefront of a new wave of local entrepreneurs. We&#8217;re inspired every day by stories of our merchants who started from selling food from their kitchen, but are now running retail stores with commercial kitchens. Our mission is to transform local businesses and empower business owners to pursue their passion.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Many of Cococart\u2019s merchants are just like him, he said. The pandemic created a new generation of independent business owners, and they represent a fast-growing segment in e-commerce. What\u2019s also helping is that people are now more used to ordering online, a behavior Low doesn\u2019t see going away.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cLike myself, many people who lost their jobs turned to side hustles online, which then became their main source of income,\u201d Low added. \u201cThese entrepreneurs realized that running their own business was both more profitable and fulfilling than working for others.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Since its launch, Cococart is a profitable company, with over 20,000 merchants in 90 countries signed up that have collectively taken over 500,000 orders and earned more than $15 million.<\/p>\n<p>For example, one of the company\u2019s top merchants is <a href=\"https:\/\/indocinfood.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">INDOCIN<\/a>, a company providing on-demand artisan Indonesian cuisine. Low said when the owner started with Cococart a year ago, she was selling her homemade food from her kitchen. Today, she employs a team of 24 and owns a retail outlet.<\/p>\n<p>In 2021 alone, Cococart grew its merchant count 30 times and customer growth by 46 times, according to Low. During that same time, the company grew the team from just the two founders to 22 people across 12 countries.<\/p>\n<p>To keep the momentum going, Cococart raised $4.2 million from Forerunner Ventures and Sequoia, with additional investors including Y Combinator, Uncommon Capital, Soma Capital, Liquid 2 Ventures, Fitbit CEO James Park and Curated CEO Eduardo Vivas.<\/p>\n<p>Low intends to use the new funding to continue hiring and customer acquisition.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe\u2019re just getting started,\u201d he added. \u201cOur goal is to define the next generation of commerce. There are still so many challenges in starting and running a business that we want to solve, from deliveries to supply chain to financing. We see a massive opportunity in front of us and we want to bring Cococart to 200 million businesses worldwide.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"l6Ee3sIGvj\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/4-trends-that-will-define-e-commerce-in-2022\/\">4 trends that will define e-commerce in 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;4 trends that will define e-commerce in 2022&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" store","slug":"online-store","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576921178"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576921178"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576921178"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576921178"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576921178"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576607849,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/order-management\/","name":"order management","slug":"order-management","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576607849"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576607849"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576607849"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576607849"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576607849"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2275783,"date":"2022-02-24T06:00:30","date_gmt":"2022-02-24T14:00:30","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2275783"},"modified":"2022-02-24T10:52:35","modified_gmt":"2022-02-24T18:52:35","slug":"anyroad-helps-brands-measure-customer-experiences","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/24\/anyroad-helps-brands-measure-customer-experiences\/","title":{"rendered":"AnyRoad helps brands measure customer experiences"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">We were stuck inside for so long over the past two years that now when we go anywhere, we want it to be an experience. <a href=\"http:\/\/www.anyroad.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">AnyRoad<\/a>, an eight-year-old San Francisco-based company, wants to help brands make sure we have them, while also building stronger relationships with customers.<\/p>\n<p>You might be asking yourself, \u201cHaven\u2019t I heard of a travel company with the name AnyRoad?\u201d and you would be right. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/04\/26\/anyroad\/\">TechCrunch reported on the company back in 2013<\/a> when it was a custom tour company.<\/p>\n<p>However, AnyRoad pivoted about four-and-a-half years ago to be one of the first companies to do \u201cexperience relationship management,\u201d a phrase that co-founders, and brothers, Jonathan Yaffe and Daniel Yaffe coined with Salesforce CEO Marc Benioff, who is one of the company\u2019s early investors.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2275783\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>\u201cWe were pounding our heads against the wall to build a platform to democratize experiences, which initially put us in the travel space,\u201d Jonathan Yaffe told TechCrunch. \u201cWe knew it wasn\u2019t going to be a venture-scaleable company, but we were sitting on a mountain of data and realized we could predict experiences that could change the fate of businesses.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Much of Yaffe\u2019s background in experiences came from being initially in cognitive neuroscience, learning about behavioral data. However, he decided not to spend his life in a research lab, and instead got a job on the marketing team at Red Bull. This was two decades or so ago when Red Bull had just come to the U.S.<\/p>\n<p>He recalls the company spending millions on experiences to get Red Bull into people\u2019s hands. However, rather than sink money into digital marketing \u2014 an area that was oversaturated even then \u2014 Red Bull concentrated on events where people could bring their group of friends, have a good time and be eager to try a new drink. It ended up being experiences that created a bond between Red Bull and its customers and changed customers\u2019 relationship to the brand and purchase habits, Yaffe said.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>That is the kind of relationship AnyRoad is helping any brand create with its customers. And data shows this is the direction brands are going: the experience economy is booming now that we are all going out again, and 81% of brands say their <a href=\"https:\/\/www.eventmarketer.com\/article\/15-data-points-state-of-experiential\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">event and experiential budgets<\/a> will \u201cmatch or exceed\u201d pre-pandemic levels in 2022.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2275817\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2275817\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-2275817\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"Jonathan Yaffe, AnyRoad\" width=\"300\" height=\"296\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg 1676w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=150,148 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=300,296 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=768,757 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=680,670 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=1536,1514 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/jonathan-headshot.jpg?resize=96,96 96w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2275817\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">AnyRoad co-founder and CEO Jonathan Yaffe. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> AnyRoad<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>However, when it&#8217;s a big party, brands don\u2019t often know everyone who is attending, which leads to limited return on investment and actionable insights. AnyRoad provides that insight with software. For example, for its craft store client Michaels, AnyRoad\u2019s software creates the arts and crafts class schedule, manages ticket sales and payments and, if the class is online, facilitates the video conferencing. It also pulls in all of the consumer data from the classes, then applies machine learning and natural language processing to provide qualitative feedback.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt turns into a holistic view for them of their community and helps increase revenue,\u201d Yaffe added. \u201cExperiences make us happier than buying things, and research shows it. Some might say that retail is dead, but experiential retail is booming.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PmF9QlXIdP\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/04\/26\/anyroad\/\">Travel Startup AnyRoad Tries To Provide Anything But Your Typical Travel Tour<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Travel Startup AnyRoad Tries To Provide Anything But Your Typical Travel Tour&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/04\/26\/anyroad\/embed\/#?secret=WdT5eDGMaJ#?secret=PmF9QlXIdP\" data-secret=\"PmF9QlXIdP\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>The shift of more brands becoming experiential businesses drove AnyRoad to go after a $47 million Series B funding round, led by funds and accounts managed by BlackRock, with participation from Andreessen Horowitz, Runa Capital, Kaiser Permanente, other existing investors Rally Ventures, Precursor Ventures and Day One Ventures, and new investors Commonfund and Corner Ventures.<\/p>\n<p>The latest funding round gives the company total investment of $66.2 million, which includes a $9.2 million Series A round in 2020 and $10 million Series A extension in 2021.<\/p>\n<p>Companies ramping up their experiential budgets is resulting in AnyRoad seeing a ton of growth, Yaffe said. The company tripled its top line revenue in 2021, and brought in new brands like Diageo, Beam Suntory, Unilever and Anheuser-Busch. AnyRoad is now working with over 400 brands delivering 200,000 virtual, in-person or hybrid experiences every month.<\/p>\n<p>The new funding will go toward scaling the company\u2019s go-to-market team, product development, data insights, customer data experience and predictive modeling. AnyRoad is also exploring other verticals like web3\u2019s impact on a brand\u2019s ability to interact with its customer base, not on Discord, but with experiences like the Bored Ape Yacht Club and conferences, Yaffe said.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe experience economy is stronger than ever,\u201d he added. \u201cIt is interesting to see the scope of organizations that are now looking at experiences as the primary way to engage with their consumer base. Brands we never expected to be experiential are now creating programs and coming to us.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qbgCRO6xwt\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/01\/virtual-events-startups-have-high-hopes-for-after-the-pandemic\/\">Virtual events startups have high hopes for after the pandemic<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Virtual events startups have high hopes for after the pandemic&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/01\/virtual-events-startups-have-high-hopes-for-after-the-pandemic\/embed\/#?secret=QACMSWpQFL#?secret=qbgCRO6xwt\" data-secret=\"qbgCRO6xwt\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Brands don\u2019t often know everyone who is attending their big events, which leads to limited return on investment and actionable insights.
